     <p>
      <b>
       Carole King
      </b>
      (born February 9, 1942) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      -winning New York-born
      <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">
       composer
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter" title="Singer-songwriter">
       singer-songwriter
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      King's career began in the 1960s when she, along with her then husband
      <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Goffin" title="Gerry Goffin">
       Gerry Goffin
      </a>
      , wrote more than two dozen chart hits for numerous artists, many of which have become standards. She has continued writing for other artists since then. King's success as a performer in her own right did not come until the 1970s, when she sang her own songs, accompanying herself on the piano, in a series of albums and concerts. After experiencing commercial disappointment with her debut album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Writer_(album)" title="Writer (album)">
        Writer
       </a>
      </i>
      , King scored her breakthrough with the album
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapestry_(Carole_King_album)" title="Tapestry (Carole King album)">
        Tapestry
       </a>
      </i>
      , which topped the U.S. album chart for 15 weeks in 1971 and remained on the charts for more than six years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2000,
      <a href="/wiki/Joel_Whitburn" title="Joel Whitburn">
       Joel Whitburn
      </a>
      , a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">
        Billboard
       </a>
      </i>
      pop music researcher, named King the most successful female songwriter of 195599 because she wrote or co-wrote 118 pop hits on the
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       Hot 100
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She has written 61 hits on the UK charts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005 music historian Stuart Devoy found her the most successful female songwriter on the UK singles charts 19522005.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      King has made 25 solo albums, the most successful being
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      , which held the record for most weeks at No. 1 by a female artist for more than 20 years until broken by
      <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">
       Whitney Houston
      </a>
      (for the soundtrack album
      <i>
       The Bodyguard
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Her most recent non-compilation album was
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Live_at_the_Troubadour_(Carole_King_and_James_Taylor)" title="Live at the Troubadour (Carole King and James Taylor)">
        Live at the Troubadour
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2010, a collaboration with
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      that reached number 4 on the charts in its first week and has sold over 600,000 copies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic.com_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-allmusic.com-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      She has won four
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Awards
      </a>
      and was inducted into the
      <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">
       Songwriters Hall of Fame
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">
       Rock and Roll Hall of Fame
      </a>
      for her songwriting. She is the recipient of the 2013
      <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
       Library of Congress
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Gershwin_Prize" title="Gershwin Prize">
       Gershwin Prize for Popular Song
      </a>
      , the first woman to be so honored.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_.2760s_song-writing_.281942.E2.80.931969.29">
       Early life and '60s song-writing (19421969)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and '60s song-writing (19421969)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      King was born
      <b>
       Carol Joan Klein
      </b>
      in February 1942, to a Jewish family, in
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">
       Manhattan
      </a>
      . Her mother, Eugenia (ne Cammer), was a teacher, and her father, Sidney N. Klein, was a firefighter.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She grew up in
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      learning the piano when she was four years old, and appearing on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Horn_and_Hardart_Children%27s_Hour" title="The Horn and Hardart Children's Hour">
        The Horn and Hardart Children's Hour
       </a>
      </i>
      with a school friend, performing "
      <a href="/wiki/If_I_Knew_You_Were_Comin%27_I%27d%27ve_Baked_a_Cake" title="If I Knew You Were Comin' I'd've Baked a Cake">
       If I Knew You Were Comin' I'd've Baked a Cake
      </a>
      " when she was eight.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Madison_High_School_(New_York)" title="James Madison High School (New York)">
       James Madison High School
      </a>
      in the 1950s, Carol Klein changed her name to Carole King, formed a band called the Co-Sines, and made demo records with her friend
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Simon" title="Paul Simon">
       Paul Simon
      </a>
      for $25 a session.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-biography-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Her first official recording was the promotional single "The Right Girl", released by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC-Paramount" title="ABC-Paramount">
       ABC-Paramount
      </a>
      in 1958, which she wrote and sang to an arrangement by
      <a href="/wiki/Don_Costa" title="Don Costa">
       Don Costa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She attended
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queens_College,_New_York" title="Queens College, New York">
       Queens College
      </a>
      , where she met
      <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Goffin" title="Gerry Goffin">
       Gerry Goffin
      </a>
      , who was to become her song-writing partner. When she was 17, they married in a Jewish ceremony on Long Island in August 1959 after King had become pregnant with her first daughter,
      <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
       Louise
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weller_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-weller-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They left college and took daytime jobs, Goffin working as an assistant chemist and King as a secretary, while writing songs together in the evening at an office belonging to
      <a href="/wiki/Don_Kirshner" title="Don Kirshner">
       Don Kirshner
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Aldon_Music" title="Aldon Music">
       Aldon Music
      </a>
      at 1650 Broadway opposite the
      <a href="/wiki/Brill_Building" title="Brill Building">
       Brill Building
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Neil_Sedaka" title="Neil Sedaka">
       Neil Sedaka
      </a>
      , who dated King when he was still in high school,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      had a hit in 1959 with "
      <a href="/wiki/Oh!_Carol" title="Oh! Carol">
       Oh! Carol
      </a>
      "; Goffin took the tune and wrote the playful response "Oh! Neil", which King recorded and released as a single the same year; the B-side contained the Goffin-King song "A Very Special Boy".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perone_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-perone-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The single was not a success;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      however, after writing "
      <a href="/wiki/Will_You_Love_Me_Tomorrow" title="Will You Love Me Tomorrow">
       Will You Love Me Tomorrow
      </a>
      ", which topped the American charts in 1960 in a recording by
      <a href="/wiki/The_Shirelles" title="The Shirelles">
       the Shirelles
      </a>
      , becoming the first No.1 hit by a black girl group,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Goffin and King gave up the daytime jobs in order to concentrate on writing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Will You Love Me Tomorrow" has gone on to become a standard, recorded by numerous artists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During the sixties, with King writing the music and Goffin the lyrics, they wrote
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_songs_written_by_Goffin_and_King" title="List of songs written by Goffin and King">
       a string of classic songs
      </a>
      for a variety of artists,.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caroleking_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-caroleking-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For part of this period King and Goffin were the songwriting team behind Don Kirshner's
      <a href="/wiki/Dimension_Records" title="Dimension Records">
       Dimension Records
      </a>
      , which produced songs including "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chains_(The_Cookies_song)" title="Chains (The Cookies song)">
       Chains
      </a>
      " (later covered by
      <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">
       the Beatles
      </a>
      ), "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Loco-Motion" title="The Loco-Motion">
       The Loco-Motion
      </a>
      " for their babysitter
      <a href="/wiki/Little_Eva" title="Little Eva">
       Little Eva
      </a>
      and "
      <a href="/wiki/It_Might_as_Well_Rain_Until_September" title="It Might as Well Rain Until September">
       It Might as Well Rain Until September
      </a>
      " which King recorded herselfher first (and only Sixties) hit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other songs of this period include: "Half Way To Paradise" [Tony Orlando, covered by Billy Fury in U.K.], "
      <a href="/wiki/Take_Good_Care_of_My_Baby" title="Take Good Care of My Baby">
       Take Good Care of My Baby
      </a>
      " for
      <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Vee" title="Bobby Vee">
       Bobby Vee
      </a>
      ; "
      <a href="/wiki/Up_on_the_Roof_(song)" title="Up on the Roof (song)">
       Up on the Roof
      </a>
      " for
      <a href="/wiki/The_Drifters" title="The Drifters">
       the Drifters
      </a>
      ; "
      <a href="/wiki/I%27m_into_Something_Good" title="I'm into Something Good">
       I'm into Something Good
      </a>
      " for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earl-Jean" title="Earl-Jean">
       Earl-Jean
      </a>
      (later covered by
      <a href="/wiki/Herman%27s_Hermits" title="Herman's Hermits">
       Herman's Hermits
      </a>
      ); "
      <a href="/wiki/Pleasant_Valley_Sunday" title="Pleasant Valley Sunday">
       Pleasant Valley Sunday
      </a>
      " for
      <a href="/wiki/The_Monkees" title="The Monkees">
       the Monkees
      </a>
      (inspired by their move to suburban
      <a href="/wiki/West_Orange,_New_Jersey" title="West Orange, New Jersey">
       West Orange, New Jersey
      </a>
      );
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and "
      <a href="/wiki/(You_Make_Me_Feel_Like)_A_Natural_Woman" title="(You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman">
       (You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman
      </a>
      " for
      <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">
       Aretha Franklin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <span id="The_City">
      </span>
     </p>
     <p>
      By 1968, Goffin and King were divorced and were starting to lose contact.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weller_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-weller-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      King moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Laurel_Canyon,_Los_Angeles" title="Laurel Canyon, Los Angeles">
       Laurel Canyon
      </a>
      in Los Angeles with her two daughters and formed the City, a music trio consisting of Charles Larkey, her future husband, on bass,
      <a href="/wiki/Danny_Kortchmar" title="Danny Kortchmar">
       Danny Kortchmar
      </a>
      on guitar and vocals, and King on piano and vocals.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caroleking_29-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-caroleking-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The City produced one album,
      <i>
       Now That Everything's Been Said
      </i>
      in 1968, but King's reluctance to perform live meant sales were slow,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and after a change of distributors it got deleted early, and the group disbanded in 1969.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-now_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-now-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Seventies_singer-songwriter_and_Tapestry_.281970.E2.80.931979.29">
       Seventies singer-songwriter and
       <i>
        Tapestry
       </i>
       (19701979)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seventies singer-songwriter and Tapestry (19701979)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1030" data-file-width="834" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/19/Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg/220px-Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/19/Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg/330px-Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/19/Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg/440px-Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King_-_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        King circa 1977
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      While in Laurel Canyon, King met
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Joni_Mitchell" title="Joni Mitchell">
       Joni Mitchell
      </a>
      as well as Toni Stern, with whom she would collaborate on songs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_16-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-biography-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      King made her first solo album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Writer_(album)" title="Writer (album)">
        Writer
       </a>
      </i>
      , in 1970 for Lou Adler's Ode label, with Taylor playing acoustic guitar and providing backing vocals. It peaked at number 84 in the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      Top 200. King followed
      <i>
       Writer
      </i>
      in 1971 with
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapestry_(Carole_King_album)" title="Tapestry (Carole King album)">
        Tapestry
       </a>
      </i>
      , featuring recent solo compositions as well as reinterpretations of two Goffin-King songs, "Will You Love Me Tomorrow" and "
      <a href="/wiki/(You_Make_Me_Feel_Like)_A_Natural_Woman" title="(You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman">
       (You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      The album was recorded in an overlap with Taylor's
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mud_Slide_Slim" title="Mud Slide Slim">
        Mud Slide Slim
       </a>
      </i>
      on which King,
      <a href="/wiki/Danny_Kortchmar" title="Danny Kortchmar">
       Danny Kortchmar
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Joni_Mitchell" title="Joni Mitchell">
       Joni Mitchell
      </a>
      appeared as they did on
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      , with both albums including "
      <a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Friend" title="You've Got a Friend">
       You've Got a Friend
      </a>
      ", which was a number 1 hit for Taylor; King said in a 1972 interview, that she "didn't write it with James or anybody really specifically in mind. But when James heard it he really liked it and wanted to record it".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      was an instant success. With numerous hit singles  including a
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
      </a>
      No.1 with "
      <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Too_Late_(Carole_King_song)" title="It's Too Late (Carole King song)">
       It's Too Late
      </a>
      " 
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      held the No.1 spot for 15 consecutive weeks, remained on the charts for nearly six years, and has sold over 25million copies worldwide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The album garnered four
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">
       Grammy Awards
      </a>
      including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Album_of_the_Year_(Grammy)" title="Album of the Year (Grammy)">
       Album of the Year
      </a>
      ; Best Pop Vocal Performance, Female; Record of the Year ("It's Too Late," lyrics by Toni Stern); and
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">
       Song of the Year
      </a>
      , with King becoming the first woman to win the award ("
      <a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Friend" title="You've Got a Friend">
       You've Got a Friend
      </a>
      "). The album appeared on
      <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">
       Rolling Stone
      </a>
      's "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="500 Greatest Albums of All Time">
       500 Greatest Albums of All Time
      </a>
      " list at number 36.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, "It's Too Late" was placed at number 469 on Rolling Stone's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/500_Greatest_Songs_of_All_Time" title="500 Greatest Songs of All Time">
       500 Greatest Songs of All Time
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Music_(Carole_King_album)" title="Music (Carole King album)">
        Carole King: Music
       </a>
      </i>
      was released in December 1971, certified gold on December 9, 1971. It entered the top ten at 8, becoming the first of many weeks
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Carole King: Music
      </i>
      simultaneously occupied the top 10. The following week it rose to No.3 and finally to No.1 on January 1, 1972, staying there for three weeks. The album also spawned a top 10 hit, "Sweet Seasons" (US No.9 and AC No.2).
      <i>
       Carole King: Music
      </i>
      stayed on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      pop album charts for 44 weeks and was eventually certified platinum.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhymes_and_Reasons_(Carole_King_album)" title="Rhymes and Reasons (Carole King album)">
        Rhymes and Reasons
       </a>
      </i>
      (1972), and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Carole_King_album)" title="Fantasy (Carole King album)">
        Fantasy
       </a>
      </i>
      (1973) followed, each earning gold certifications.
      <i>
       Rhymes and Reasons
      </i>
      produced another hit, "
      <a href="/wiki/Been_to_Canaan" title="Been to Canaan">
       Been to Canaan
      </a>
      " (US No.24 and AC No.1), and
      <i>
       Fantasy
      </i>
      produced two hits, "Believe in Humanity" (US No.28) and "Corazon" (US No.37 and AC No.5), as well as another song that charted on the Hot 100, "You Light Up My Life" (US No.68 and AC No.6).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1973, King performed a free concert in New York City's
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">
       Central Park
      </a>
      with 100,000 attending.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 1974, King released her album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Wrap_Around_Joy" title="Wrap Around Joy">
        Wrap Around Joy
       </a>
       ,
      </i>
      which was certified gold on October 16, 1974, and entered the top ten at 7 on October 19, 1974. Two weeks later it reached 1 and stayed there one week.
      <i>
       Wrap Around Joy
      </i>
      spawned two hits. "
      <a href="/wiki/Jazzman" title="Jazzman">
       Jazzman
      </a>
      " was a single and reached 2 on November 9 but fell out of the top ten the next week. "
      <a href="/wiki/Nightingale_(Carole_King_song)" title="Nightingale (Carole King song)">
       Nightingale
      </a>
      ", a single on December 17, went to No. 9 on March 1, 1975.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1975, King scored songs for the animated TV production of
      <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Sendak" title="Maurice Sendak">
       Maurice Sendak
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Really_Rosie" title="Really Rosie">
        Really Rosie
       </a>
      </i>
      , released as an album by the same name, with lyrics by Sendak.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_(Carole_King_album)" title="Thoroughbred (Carole King album)">
        Thoroughbred
       </a>
      </i>
      (1976) was the last studio album she made under the Ode label.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waddy_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-waddy-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition to enlisting her long-time friends such as
      <a href="/wiki/David_Crosby" title="David Crosby">
       David Crosby
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Graham_Nash" title="Graham Nash">
       Graham Nash
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Waddy_Wachtel" title="Waddy Wachtel">
       Waddy Wachtel
      </a>
      , King reunited with Gerry Goffin to write four songs for the album. Their partnership continued intermittently. King also did a promotional tour for the album in 1976.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1977, King collaborated with another songwriter
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rick_Evers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rick Evers (page does not exist)">
       Rick Evers
      </a>
      on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Simple_Things_(Carole_King_album)" title="Simple Things (Carole King album)">
        Simple Things
       </a>
      </i>
      , the first release with a new label distributed by
      <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">
       Capitol Records
      </a>
      . Shortly after that King and Evers were married; he died of a cocaine
      <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">
       overdose
      </a>
      one year later, while King and daughter Sherry were in
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       Simple Things
      </i>
      was her first album that failed to reach the top 10 on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      since
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      , and it was her last Gold-certified record by the RIAA, except a compilation entitled
      <i>
       Her Greatest Hits
      </i>
      the following year, and
      <i>
       Live at the Troubadour
      </i>
      in 2010.
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite its Gold-certified record status,
      <i>
       Simple Things
      </i>
      was named "The Worst Album of 1977" by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Neither
      <i>
       Welcome Home
      </i>
      (1978), her debut as a co-producer on an album, nor
      <i>
       Touch the Sky
      </i>
      (1979), reached the top 100.
      <i>
       Pearls  The Songs of Goffin and King
      </i>
      (1980) yielded a hit single, an updated version of "One Fine Day".
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life_and_work_.281982.E2.80.93present.29">
       Later life and work (1982present)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later life and work (1982present)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="981" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Carole_King.jpg/220px-Carole_King.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Carole_King.jpg/330px-Carole_King.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Carole_King.jpg/440px-Carole_King.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Carole King performing aboard
        <a href="/wiki/USS_Harry_S._Truman" title="USS Harry S. Truman">
         USS
         <i>
          Harry S. Truman
         </i>
        </a>
        in the Mediterranean in 2000
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      King moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">
       Atlantic Records
      </a>
      for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/One_to_One_(Carole_King_album)" title="One to One (Carole King album)">
        One to One
       </a>
      </i>
      (1982), and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Speeding_Time" title="Speeding Time">
        Speeding Time
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1983, which was a reunion with
      <i>
       Tapestry
      </i>
      -era producer
      <a href="/wiki/Lou_Adler" title="Lou Adler">
       Lou Adler
      </a>
      . In 1983, she played piano in "Chains and Things" on the
      <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">
       B.B. King
      </a>
      album
      <i>
       Why I Sing The Blues
      </i>
      . After a well-received concert tour in 1984, journalist Catherine Foster of the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Science_Monitor" title="Christian Science Monitor">
        Christian Science Monitor
       </a>
      </i>
      dubbed King "a Queen of Rock". She also called King's performing as "all spunk and exuberance."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1985, she wrote and performed "Care-A-Lot", the theme to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Care_Bears_Movie" title="The Care Bears Movie">
        The Care Bears Movie
       </a>
      </i>
      . Also in 1985, she scored and performed (with
      <a href="/wiki/David_Sanborn" title="David Sanborn">
       David Sanborn
      </a>
      ) the soundtrack to the
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Ritt" title="Martin Ritt">
       Martin Ritt
      </a>
      -directed movie
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Murphy%27s_Romance" title="Murphy's Romance">
        Murphy's Romance
       </a>
      </i>
      . The soundtrack, again produced by Adler, included the songs "Running Lonely" and "Love For The Last Time (Theme from 'Murphy's Romance')", although a soundtrack album was apparently never officially released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-murphy-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      King made a cameo appearance in the film as Tillie, a town hall employee.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-murphy-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1989, she returned to Capitol Records and recorded
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/City_Streets_(album)" title="City Streets (album)">
        City Streets
       </a>
      </i>
      , with
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">
       Eric Clapton
      </a>
      on two tracks and
      <a href="/wiki/Branford_Marsalis" title="Branford Marsalis">
       Branford Marsalis
      </a>
      on one, followed by
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Color_of_Your_Dreams" title="Color of Your Dreams">
        Color of Your Dreams
       </a>
      </i>
      (1993), with an appearance by
      <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">
       Slash
      </a>
      . Her song, "
      <a href="/wiki/Now_and_Forever_(Carole_King_song)" title="Now and Forever (Carole King song)">
       Now and Forever
      </a>
      ", was in the opening credits to the 1992
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_picture" title="Motion picture">
       movie
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_League_of_Their_Own" title="A League of Their Own">
        A League of Their Own
       </a>
      </i>
      , and was nominated for a
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perone_24-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-perone-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1988, she starred in the off-Broadway production
      <i>
       A Minor Incident
      </i>
      , and in 1994, she played Mrs Johnstone on Broadway in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Blood_Brothers_(musical)" title="Blood Brothers (musical)">
        Blood Brothers
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 1996, she appeared in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Beach_Memoirs" title="Brighton Beach Memoirs">
        Brighton Beach Memoirs
       </a>
      </i>
      in Ireland, directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sheridan" title="Peter Sheridan">
       Peter Sheridan
      </a>
      . In 1991, she wrote with
      <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">
       Mariah Carey
      </a>
      the song "
      <a href="/wiki/If_It%27s_Over" title="If It's Over">
       If It's Over
      </a>
      ", for Carey's second album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey album)">
        Emotions
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 1996, she wrote "Wall Of Smiles/Torre De Marfil" with
      <a href="/wiki/Soraya_(musician)" title="Soraya (musician)">
       Soraya
      </a>
      for her 1997 album of the same title.
     </p>
     <p>
      Early 1991 saw King's song "
      <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Too_Late_(Carole_King_song)" title="It's Too Late (Carole King song)">
       It's Too Late
      </a>
      " covered by
      <a href="/wiki/Dina_Carroll" title="Dina Carroll">
       Dina Carroll
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Quartz_(band)" title="Quartz (band)">
       Quartz
      </a>
      album
      <i>
       Perfect Timing
      </i>
      . The cover topped the dance charts worldwide and reached No.8 in the UK Singles Chart in 1991. It was hoped that King would appear in the filming of the video for the song but she declined, citing her heavy tour schedule at that time.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1997, King wrote and recorded backing vocals on "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Reason_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="The Reason (Celine Dion song)">
       The Reason
      </a>
      " for
      <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">
       Celine Dion
      </a>
      on her album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">
        Let's Talk About Love
       </a>
      </i>
      . The song sold worldwide, including one million in France. It went to number 1 in France, 11 in the UK, and 13 in Ireland. The pair performed a duet on the first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VH1_Divas_Live" title="VH1 Divas Live">
       VH1 Divas Live
      </a>
      benefit concert. King also performed her "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_A_Friend" title="You've Got A Friend">
       You've Got A Friend
      </a>
      " with Celine Dion,
      <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">
       Gloria Estefan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">
       Shania Twain
      </a>
      as well as "
      <a href="/wiki/(You_Make_Me_Feel_Like)_A_Natural_Woman" title="(You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman">
       (You Make Me Feel Like) A Natural Woman
      </a>
      " with
      <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">
       Aretha Franklin
      </a>
      and others, including Mariah Carey. In 1998, King wrote "Anyone at All", and performed it in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_Mail" title="You've Got Mail">
        You've Got Mail
       </a>
      </i>
      , starring
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">
       Tom Hanks
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Meg_Ryan" title="Meg Ryan">
       Meg Ryan
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2001, King appeared in a television ad for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gap_(clothing_retailer)" title="Gap (clothing retailer)">
       the Gap
      </a>
      , with her daughter,
      <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
       Louise Goffin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gap_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gap-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She performed a new song, "Love Makes the World", which became a title track for her studio album in autumn 2001 on her own label, Rockingale, distributed by Koch Records. The album includes songs she wrote for other artists during the mid-1990s and features Celine Dion,
      <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">
       Steven Tyler
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenneth_%22Babyface%22_Edmonds" title='Kenneth "Babyface" Edmonds'>
       Babyface
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/K.d._lang" title="K.d. lang">
       k.d. lang
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       Love Makes the World
      </i>
      went to 158 in the US and No. 86 in the UK. It also debuted on
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      s Top Independent Albums chart and Top Internet Albums chart at No. 20.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic.com_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-allmusic.com-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      An expanded edition of the album was issued six years later called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Love_Makes_the_World#Deluxe_edition" title="Love Makes the World">
        Love Makes the World Deluxe Edition
       </a>
      </i>
      . It contains a bonus disc with five additional tracks, including a remake of "Where You Lead (I Will Follow)" co-written with Toni Stern.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The same year, King and Stern wrote "Sayonara Dance", recorded by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuki_Isoya" title="Yuki Isoya">
       Yuki
      </a>
      , former lead vocalist of the Japanese band
      <a href="/wiki/Judy_and_Mary" title="Judy and Mary">
       Judy and Mary
      </a>
      , on her first solo album
      <i>
       Prismic
      </i>
      the following year. Also in 2001, King composed a song for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/All_About_Chemistry" title="All About Chemistry">
        All About Chemistry
       </a>
      </i>
      album by
      <a href="/wiki/Semisonic" title="Semisonic">
       Semisonic
      </a>
      , with the band's frontman
      <a href="/wiki/Dan_Wilson_(musician)" title="Dan Wilson (musician)">
       Dan Wilson
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      King launched her Living Room Tour in July 2004 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Auditorium_Theatre" title="Auditorium Theatre">
       Auditorium Theatre
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      . That show, along with shows at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Theater_(Los_Angeles)" title="Greek Theater (Los Angeles)">
       Greek Theater
      </a>
      in Los Angeles and the Cape Cod Melody Tent (Hyannis, Massachusetts), were recorded as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Living_Room_Tour" title="The Living Room Tour">
        The Living Room Tour
       </a>
      </i>
      in July 2005. The album sold 44,000 copies in its first week in the US, landing at 17 on the
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       200
      </a>
      , her highest-charting album since 1977. The album also charted at 51 in Australia. It has sold 330,000 copies in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In August 2006 the album re-entered the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      200 at 151.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tour stopped in Canada, Australia and New Zealand. A DVD of the tour, called
      <i>
       Welcome to My Living Room
      </i>
      , was released in October 2007.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2014" data-file-width="2179" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg/220px-You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg/330px-You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg/440px-You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:You_Can_Close_Your_Eyes_JT_CK_2010_-_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        King and
        <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
         James Taylor
        </a>
        performing during their 2010
        <a href="/wiki/Troubadour_Reunion_Tour" title="Troubadour Reunion Tour">
         Troubadour Reunion Tour
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In November 2007, King toured Japan with
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">
       Mary J. Blige
      </a>
      and Fergie from
      <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">
       The Black Eyed Peas
      </a>
      . Japanese record labels
      <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">
       Sony
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Victor_Entertainment" title="Victor Entertainment">
       Victor
      </a>
      reissued most of King's albums, including the works from the late 1970s previously unavailable on compact disc. King recorded a duet of the Goffin/King composition "
      <a href="/wiki/Time_Don%27t_Run_Out_on_Me" title="Time Don't Run Out on Me">
       Time Don't Run Out on Me
      </a>
      " with
      <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">
       Anne Murray
      </a>
      on Murray's 2007 album
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne_Murray_Duets:_Friends_and_Legends" title="Anne Murray Duets: Friends and Legends">
        Anne Murray Duets: Friends and Legends
       </a>
      </i>
      . The song had previously been recorded by Murray for her 1984 album
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_Over_Mind_(Anne_Murray_album)" title="Heart Over Mind (Anne Murray album)">
        Heart Over Mind
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010, King and
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      staged their
      <a href="/wiki/Troubadour_Reunion_Tour" title="Troubadour Reunion Tour">
       Troubadour Reunion Tour
      </a>
      together, recalling the first time they played at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Troubadour,_West_Hollywood" title="The Troubadour, West Hollywood">
       The Troubadour, West Hollywood
      </a>
      in 1970. The pair had reunited two and a half years earlier in 2007 with the band they used in 1970 to mark the club's 50th anniversary. They enjoyed it so much that they decided to take the band on the road for 2010. The touring band featured players from that original band:
      <a href="/wiki/Russ_Kunkel" title="Russ Kunkel">
       Russ Kunkel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Leland_Sklar" title="Leland Sklar">
       Leland Sklar
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Danny_Kortchmar" title="Danny Kortchmar">
       Danny Kortchmar
      </a>
      . Also present was King's son-in-law,
      <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Kondor" title="Robbie Kondor">
       Robbie Kondor
      </a>
      . King played piano and Taylor guitar on each other's songs, and they sang together some of the numbers they were both associated with. The tour began in Australia in March, returning to the United States in May. It was a major commercial success, with King playing to some of the largest audiences of her career. Total ticket sales exceeded 700,000 and the tour grossed over 59 million dollars, making it one of the most successful tours of the year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During their Troubadour Reunion Tour, Carole King released two albums, one with James Taylor. The first, released on April 27, 2010,
      <i>
       The Essential Carole King
      </i>
      , is a two-disc compilation album. The first disc features many songs Carole King has recorded, mostly her hit singles. The second disc features recordings by other artists of songs that King wrote, most of which made the top 40, and many of which reached No.1.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The second album was released on May 4, 2010 and is a collaboration of King and James Taylor called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Live_at_the_Troubadour_(Carole_King_and_James_Taylor)" title="Live at the Troubadour (Carole King and James Taylor)">
        Live at the Troubadour
       </a>
      </i>
      , which debuted at No.4 in the United States with sales of 78,000 copies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Live at the Troubadour
      </i>
      has since received a gold record from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA" title="RIAA">
       RIAA
      </a>
      for shipments of over 500,000 copies in the US and has remained on the charts for 34 weeks, currently charting at No.170 on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      200.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 22, 2010, Carole King's mother, Eugenia Gingold, died in the Hospice Care unit at Delray Medical Center in Delray Beach, Florida at the age of 94. King stated that the cause of death was congestive heart failure. Gingold's passing was reported by the Miami Herald on January 1, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the fall of 2011 she released
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Holiday_Carole" title="A Holiday Carole">
        A Holiday Carole
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which includes holiday standards and new songs written by her daughter
      <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
       Louise Goffin
      </a>
      who also is producer for the album. The album would garner a Grammy nomination for Best Traditional Pop Album.
     </p>
     <p>
      Her autobiography "
      <i>
       A Natural Woman: A Memoir
      </i>
      " was published by Grand Central in the United States on April 10, 2012. It entered the NYT best seller list at No.6.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On Thursday, May 10, 2012, it was announced that Carole King was retiring from music and that her days in music have most likely ended. King herself also doubted she would ever write another song and said that her 2010 Troubadour Reunion Tour with James Taylor was probably the last tour of her life, saying that it "was a good way to go out." King also stated that she will most likely not be writing or recording any new music.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on May 22, King wrote on her Facebook page that she never said she was actually retiring, and insisted that she was just "taking a break." Carole campaigned for Idahoan
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nicole_Lefavour&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nicole Lefavour (page does not exist)">
       Nicole Lefavour
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      in 2012. Early in December 2012, Carole received a star on the Hollywood Walk of Fame.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She was awarded the
      <a href="/wiki/Gershwin_Prize" title="Gershwin Prize">
       Gershwin Prize
      </a>
      for Popular Song by the Library of Congress
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and she had the benefit concert 'Painted Turtle - a celebration of Carole King'.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      King also did an Australian tour in February 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombings" title="Boston Marathon bombings">
       Boston Marathon bombings
      </a>
      of April 2013, she performed in Boston with
      <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">
       James Taylor
      </a>
      in order to help victims of the bombing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In late 2012, The Library of Congress announced that Carole King had been named the 2013 recipient of the prestigious Gershwin Prize for Popular Song - the first woman to receive the distinction given to songwriters for a body of work. "Carole King has been one of the most influential songwriters of our time," Librarian of Congress James H. Billington said in a statement accompanying the announcement. "For more than five decades, she has written for and been recorded by many different types of artists for a wide range of audiences, communicating with beauty and dignity the universal human emotions of love, joy, pain and loss. Her body of work reflects the spirit of the Gershwin Prize with its originality, longevity and diversity of appeal." President and Mrs. Barack Obama hosted the award concert at the
      <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
       White House
      </a>
      on May 22, 2013, with the President presenting the prize and reading the citation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June 2013 she campaigned in Massachusetts for US Representative Ed Markey, the Democratic nominee in a special election for the US Senate to succeed John Kerry who had resigned to become Secretary of State.
     </p>
     <p>
      Carole King was honored as
      <a href="/wiki/MusiCares_Person_of_the_Year" title="MusiCares Person of the Year">
       MusiCares Person of the Year
      </a>
      in January 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">
       Acting career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Acting career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      King has appeared sporadically in acting roles, notably three appearances as guest star on the TV series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gilmore_Girls" title="Gilmore Girls">
        Gilmore Girls
       </a>
      </i>
      as Sophie, the owner of the
      <a href="/wiki/Stars_Hollow" title="Stars Hollow">
       Stars Hollow
      </a>
      music store. King's song "Where You Lead (I Will Follow)" was also the theme song to the series, in a version sung with her daughter
      <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
       Louise
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      King also appeared as Mrs. Johnstone as a replacement in the original Broadway production of
      <i>
       Blood Brothers
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life_and_family">
       Personal life and family
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Personal life and family">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      King has been married four times, to
      <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Goffin" title="Gerry Goffin">
       Gerry Goffin
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Larkey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles Larkey (page does not exist)">
       Charles Larkey
      </a>
      , Rick Evers, and Rick Sorenson. In her 2012
      <a href="/wiki/Memoir" title="Memoir">
       memoir
      </a>
      <i>
       A Natural Woman
      </i>
      , King wrote that she had been physically abused by her third husband, Rick Evers, on a regular basis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Evers died of a cocaine overdose days after they broke up in 1978.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Her children are musicians
      <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
       Louise Goffin
      </a>
      and Sherry Goffin Kondor, artist
      <a href="/wiki/Molly_Larkey" title="Molly Larkey">
       Molly Larkey
      </a>
      , and Levi Larkey.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
