     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_environmental_activism">
       Political and environmental activism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Political and environmental activism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      After relocating to
      <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">
       Idaho
      </a>
      in 1977, King became involved in environmental issues. Since 1990, she has been working with the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alliance_for_the_Wild_Rockies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alliance for the Wild Rockies (page does not exist)">
       Alliance for the Wild Rockies
      </a>
      and other groups towards passage of the
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rockies_Ecosystem_Protection_Act" title="Northern Rockies Ecosystem Protection Act">
       Northern Rockies Ecosystem Protection Act
      </a>
      (NREPA). King has testified on Capitol Hill three times on behalf of NREPA: in 1994, 2007 and again in 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      King is also politically active in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" title="United States Democratic Party">
       United States Democratic Party
      </a>
      . In 2003, she began campaigning for
      <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">
       John Kerry
      </a>
      , performing in private homes for caucus delegates during the Democratic primaries. On July 29, 2004, she made a short speech and sang at the
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">
       Democratic National Convention
      </a>
      , about two hours before Kerry made his acceptance speech for the Democratic nomination for President.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      King continued her support of Kerry throughout the general election. When Kerry was named Secretary of State in 2013 she campaigned with US Representative Ed Markey, the Democratic nominee to succeed Kerry in a special election.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2008, King appeared on the March 18 episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">
        The Colbert Report
       </a>
      </i>
      , touching on her politics again. She said she was supporting
      <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">
       Hillary Clinton
      </a>
      , and said the choice had nothing to do with gender. She also said she would have no issues if
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      won the election. Before the show's conclusion, she returned to the stage to perform "I Feel the Earth Move".
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 6, 2014, she performed at a Democratic fundraiser at the
      <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Wilshire_Hotel" title="Beverly Wilshire Hotel">
       Beverly Wilshire Hotel
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California" title="Beverly Hills, California">
       Beverly Hills, California
      </a>
      , attended by Vice President
      <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">
       Joe Biden
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes_and_covers">
       Tributes and covers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tributes and covers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="489" data-file-width="739" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg/240px-Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg/360px-Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg/480px-Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg 2x" width="240"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carole_King_Boston_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        King during an interview at the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JFK_Presidential_Library" title="JFK Presidential Library">
         JFK Presidential Library
        </a>
        , Boston, Mass., April 12, 2012
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      An all-star roster of artists paid tribute to King on the 1995 album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tapestry_Revisited:_A_Tribute_to_Carole_King" title="Tapestry Revisited: A Tribute to Carole King">
        Tapestry Revisited: A Tribute to Carole King
       </a>
      </i>
      . From the album,
      <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">
       Rod Stewart
      </a>
      's version of "
      <a href="/wiki/So_Far_Away_(Carole_King_song)" title="So Far Away (Carole King song)">
       So Far Away
      </a>
      " and Celine Dion's cover of "A Natural Woman" were both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_Contemporary" title="Adult Contemporary">
       Adult Contemporary
      </a>
      chart hits. Other artists who appeared on the album included
      <a href="/wiki/Amy_Grant" title="Amy Grant">
       Amy Grant
      </a>
      ("It's Too Late"),
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Marx" title="Richard Marx">
       Richard Marx
      </a>
      ("Beautiful"),
      <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">
       Aretha Franklin
      </a>
      ("You've Got a Friend"),
      <a href="/wiki/Faith_Hill" title="Faith Hill">
       Faith Hill
      </a>
      ("Where You Lead"), and the
      <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">
       Bee Gees
      </a>
      ("Will You Love Me Tomorrow?").
     </p>
     <p>
      Former
      <a href="/wiki/The_Monkees" title="The Monkees">
       Monkee
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Micky_Dolenz" title="Micky Dolenz">
       Micky Dolenz
      </a>
      released
      <i>
       King for a Day
      </i>
      , a tribute album consisting of songs written or co-written by King, in 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album includes "
      <a href="/wiki/More_of_the_Monkees" title="More of the Monkees">
       Sometime in the Morning
      </a>
      ", a King-penned song originally recorded by the Monkees in 1967. Dolenz had previously recorded another of King's Monkees compositions, "
      <a href="/wiki/Porpoise_Song_(Theme_from_Head)" title="Porpoise Song (Theme from Head)">
       Porpoise Song
      </a>
      ", on his lullaby-themed CD
      <i>
       Micky Dolenz Puts You to Sleep
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Many other cover versions of King's work have appeared over the years. Most notably, "
      <a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Friend" title="You've Got a Friend">
       You've Got a Friend
      </a>
      " was a smash No.1 hit for James Taylor in 1971 and a top 40 hit for
      <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Flack" title="Roberta Flack">
       Roberta Flack
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Donny_Hathaway" title="Donny Hathaway">
       Donny Hathaway
      </a>
      that same year.
      <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Hayes" title="Isaac Hayes">
       Isaac Hayes
      </a>
      recorded "
      <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Too_Late_(Carole_King_song)" title="It's Too Late (Carole King song)">
       It's Too Late
      </a>
      " for his No.1 R&amp;B live album
      <i>
       Live at the Sahara Tahoe
      </i>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">
       Barbra Streisand
      </a>
      had a top 40 hit in 1972 with "
      <a href="/wiki/Where_You_Lead" title="Where You Lead">
       Where You Lead
      </a>
      " twice  by itself and as part of a live medley with "Sweet Inspiration". Streisand also covered "No Easy Way Down" in 1971, "Beautiful" and "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_A_Friend" title="You've Got A Friend">
       You've Got A Friend
      </a>
      " in 1972, and "Being At War With Each Other" in 1974. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpenters" title="Carpenters">
       Carpenters
      </a>
      , while having musical equipment installed, first heard "
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=It%27s_Gonna_Take_Some_Time_This_Time&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="It's Gonna Take Some Time This Time (page does not exist)">
       It's Gonna Take Some Time This Time
      </a>
      and liked it so much that they recorded it.
      <a href="/wiki/Helen_Reddy" title="Helen Reddy">
       Helen Reddy
      </a>
      covered two Carole King penned tunes: the first was "
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=No_Sad_Song&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="No Sad Song (page does not exist)">
       No Sad Song
      </a>
      " in 1971; the second was "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Hear_You_No_More" title="I Can't Hear You No More">
       I Can't Hear You No More
      </a>
      " in 1976.
      <a href="/wiki/The_Carpenters" title="The Carpenters">
       The Carpenters
      </a>
      recorded King's "
      <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Going_to_Take_Some_Time" title="It's Going to Take Some Time">
       It's Going to Take Some Time
      </a>
      " in 1972, and reached number 12 on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      charts.
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Carpenter_(musician)" title="Richard Carpenter (musician)">
       Richard Carpenter
      </a>
      produced a version of "You've Got A Friend" with then teen singer/actor
      <a href="/wiki/Scott_Grimes" title="Scott Grimes">
       Scott Grimes
      </a>
      in 1989.
      <a href="/wiki/Martika" title="Martika">
       Martika
      </a>
      had a number 25 hit in 1989 with her version of "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Feel_the_Earth_Move" title="I Feel the Earth Move">
       I Feel the Earth Move
      </a>
      ", and "It's Too Late" reappeared on the Adult Contemporary chart in 1995 by
      <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">
       Gloria Estefan
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ronstadt" title="Linda Ronstadt">
       Linda Ronstadt
      </a>
      recorded a new version of "
      <a href="/wiki/Oh_No_Not_My_Baby" title="Oh No Not My Baby">
       Oh No Not My Baby
      </a>
      " in 1993. Celine Dion also recorded King's song "The Reason" on her 1997 album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">
        Let's Talk About Love
       </a>
      </i>
      with Carole King singing backup and it became a million-seller and was certified Diamond in France. "Where You Lead" (lyrics by
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Toni_Stern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Toni Stern (page does not exist)">
       Toni Stern
      </a>
      ) became the title song of TV show
      <i>
       Gilmore Girls
      </i>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Moore" title="Mandy Moore">
       Mandy Moore
      </a>
      covered "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Feel_the_Earth_Move" title="I Feel the Earth Move">
       I Feel the Earth Move
      </a>
      " on her 2003 album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Coverage_(album)" title="Coverage (album)">
        Coverage
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1996, a film very loosely based on her life,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Grace_of_My_Heart" title="Grace of My Heart">
        Grace of My Heart
       </a>
       ,
      </i>
      was released. In the film an aspiring singer sacrifices her own singing career to write hit songs that launch the careers of other singers. Mirroring King's life, the film follows her from her first break, through the pain of rejection from the recording industry and a bad marriage, to her final triumph in realizing her dream to record her own hit album.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Film_biography">
       Film biography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Film biography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Grace_of_My_Heart" title="Grace of My Heart">
       Grace of My Heart
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Allison_Anders" title="Allison Anders">
       Allison Anders
      </a>
      wrote and directed her 1996 sleeper hit
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Grace_of_My_Heart" title="Grace of My Heart">
        Grace of My Heart
       </a>
      </i>
      loosely basing the lead character upon many widely documented facts about King's life as well as a then-current music scene on which it is laid. The story is fleshed out with material equally loosely based upon her songwriting colleagues, the singers for whom they wrote their material and their various producers involved in the creative environment anchored at the
      <a href="/wiki/Brill_Building" title="Brill Building">
       Brill Building
      </a>
      from 195864 and from the California music scene from 1965-71.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadway_musical_biography">
       Broadway musical biography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Broadway musical biography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Beautiful:_The_Carole_King_Musical" title="Beautiful: The Carole King Musical">
       Beautiful: The Carole King Musical
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A musical version of King's life and career debuted in pre-
      <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">
       Broadway
      </a>
      tryouts in September 2013, in
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      , titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Beautiful:_The_Carole_King_Musical" title="Beautiful: The Carole King Musical">
        Beautiful: The Carole King Musical
       </a>
      </i>
      . It starred
      <a href="/wiki/Jessie_Mueller" title="Jessie Mueller">
       Jessie Mueller
      </a>
      in the title role.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Previews on Broadway began on November 21, 2013 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim_Theatre" title="Stephen Sondheim Theatre">
       Stephen Sondheim Theatre
      </a>
      , with the official opening on January 12, 2014. The book is by
      <a href="/wiki/Douglas_McGrath" title="Douglas McGrath">
       Douglas McGrath
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Reviews were mixed, but generally warm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jessie Mueller won the
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Actress_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Actress in a Musical">
       Tony Award for Best Performance by an Actress in a Leading Role in a Musical
      </a>
      for her portrayal of King, and Brian Ronan won the
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Sound_Design" title="Tony Award for Best Sound Design">
       Tony Award for Best Sound Design of a Musical
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">
       Recognition
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Recognition">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In 1987, Goffin and King were inducted into the Songwriters Hall of Fame.
      </li>
      <li>
       In 1988, Goffin and King received the National Academy of Songwriters Lifetime Achievement Award.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weller_19-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-weller-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 1990, King was inducted, along with Goffin, into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame in the non-performer category for her songwriting achievements.
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2002, King was given the "Johnny Mercer Award" by the Songwriters Hall of Fame.
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2004, Goffin and King were awarded the
       <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Trustees_Award" title="Grammy Trustees Award">
        Grammy Trustees Award
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       King was inducted into the
       <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Long Island Music Hall of Fame">
        Long Island Music Hall of Fame
       </a>
       in 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         82
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2012 (December 3), King received the 2,486th star on the
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">
        Hollywood Walk of Fame
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       In February 2013, King was awarded the
       <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">
        Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       On Tuesday, May 21, 2013, the
       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
        Library of Congress
       </a>
       hosted an invitation-only concert at their Coolidge Auditorium in honor of Carole King. The all-star tribute included performances by
       <a href="/wiki/Siedah_Garrett" title="Siedah Garrett">
        Siedah Garrett
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colbie_Caillat" title="Colbie Caillat">
        Colbie Caillat
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gian_Marco" title="Gian Marco">
        Gian Marco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Lynne" title="Shelby Lynne">
        Shelby Lynne
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Patti_Austin" title="Patti Austin">
        Patti Austin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Sandoval" title="Arturo Sandoval">
        Arturo Sandoval
       </a>
       and King's daughter,
       <a href="/wiki/Louise_Goffin" title="Louise Goffin">
        Louise Goffin
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         83
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       On the following night, May 22, 2013, at the White House, King was joined by other star performers including James Taylor,
       <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">
        Gloria Estefan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Emeli_Sand%C3%A9" title="Emeli Sand">
        Emeli Sand
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trisha_Yearwood" title="Trisha Yearwood">
        Trisha Yearwood
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jesse_McCartney" title="Jesse McCartney">
        Jesse McCartney
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">
        Billy Joel
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         84
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
        President Barack Obama
       </a>
       presented Carole King with the fourth
       <a href="/wiki/Gershwin_Prize" title="Gershwin Prize">
        Library of Congress Gershwin Prize for Popular Song
       </a>
       , the first awarded to a woman composer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White_House_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-White_House-85">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         85
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The White House concert and awards ceremony capped off two days of events celebrating Carole King.
      </li>
     </ul>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Certifications">
       Certifications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carole_King&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Certifications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The years given are the years the albums and singles were released, and not necessarily the years in which they achieved their peak.
     </p>

       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

      <li>

        </a>
       </i>
       (No.1)

      <li>

       <i>

         Music
        </a>
       </i>
       (No.1)
      </li>
      <li>
       1972 
       <i>
